## 10.6 1G Ethernet Controller
### 10.6.1 Overview
The Ethernet Controller (also referred to as the Ethernet AVB, ETHER_QOS, or Ethernet MAC (Media Access Controller)) enables a host to transmit and receive data over the Ethernet in compliance with the IEEE 802.3-2008 standard. It also supports standards related to Audio Video Bridging (also called Time Sensitive Networking) and is primarily intended for use in automotive applications, but it may also be used as a general-purpose Ethernet interface.
#### 10.6.1.1 Standards Compliance
The Ethernet Controller is compliant with the following standards: IEEE 802.3-2008 for Ethernet MAC IEEE 1588-2008 for precision-networked clock synchronization IEEE 802.3az-2010 for Energy Efficient Ethernet (EEE) IEEE 802.1as-201, timing, and synchronization for time-sensitive applications in bridged LANs IEEE 802.1Qat and IEEE 802.1Qav standards, Virtual Bridged LANs IEEE 1722-2011, Layer 2-transport protocol for time-sensitive apps in bridged LANs IEEE 802.1Q, VLAN tag filtering of Rx packets RGMII specification version 2.0 from HP/Marvell IEEE 802.1Qbv-2015 for Enhancements to Scheduling Traffic IEEE802.1Qbu/802.3br for Frame preemption and Interspersing Express IEEE 802.1AE-2018 for MACSEC Media Access Control Security (MACsec)

1G Ethernet Controller
**Figure 10.24 High-Level Block Diagram**
#### 10.6.1.2 Ethernet Controller Features
The Ethernet Controller supports the following features: One channel (channel 0) for legacy, best-effort Ethernet traffic on transmit interface. Support for a maximum of eight queues at 100 Mbps and 1,000 Mbps. Support for jumbo frames of up to 16 KB Support for an RGMII 1.8 V interface to an external Ethernet PHY at 10, 100, and 1,000 Mbps data transfer rates Support for serial Management interface MDIO and MDC. Forwarding Rx multicast/broadcast packets to multiple queues. Hardware virtualization capable of one (Hypervisor) + four (Guest OS) windows, to share the Ethernet Controller between up to four virtual machines. Audio synchronized to network time Low predictable latency for audio packet processing. Capable of managing "class A" network traffic from a secure processor using the integrated secure processors
##### 10.6.1.2.1 Mac Features
Separate transmission, reception, and control interfaces to the application Configurable big-endian and little-endian mode for Transmit and Receive paths Half-duplex operation: When Half duplex is enabled, only single channel can be used (channel 0). CSMA/CD Protocol support

1G Ethernet Controller Flow control using back pressure support (based on implementation-specific whitepapers and UNH Ethernet Clause 4 MAC Test Suite - Annex D) Packet bursting and packet extension in 1,000 Mbps half-duplex operation Full-duplex flow-control operations (IEEE 802.3x Pause packets and Priority flow control). Network statistics with RMON or MIB Counters (RFC2819/RFC2665) Ethernet packet timestamping as described in IEEE 1588-2002 and IEEE 1588-2008 (64-bit timestamps given in the Tx or Rx status of PTP packet). Both one-step and two-step timestamping are supported in Tx direction. MDIO (Clause 22 and Clause 45) master interface for PHY device configuration and management
##### 10.6.1.2.2 Tx and Rx Features
Separate transmission, reception, and control interfaces to the application Configurable big-endian and little-endian mode for Transmit and Receive paths Half-duplex operation: When Half duplex is enabled, only single channel can be used (channel 0). CSMA/CD Protocol support Flow control using backpressure support (based on implementation-specific whitepapers and UNH Ethernet Clause 4-MAC Test Suite - Annex D) Packet bursting and packet extension in 1,000 Mbps half-duplex operation Full-duplex flow-control operations (IEEE 802.3x Pause packets and Priority flow control) Network statistics with RMON or MIB Counters (RFC2819/RFC2665) Ethernet packet timestamping as described in IEEE 1588-2002 and IEEE 1588-2008 (64-bit timestamps given in the Tx or Rx status of PTP packet). Both one-step and two-step timestamping are supported in Tx direction. Flexibility to control the Pulse-Per-Second (PPS) output signal (ptp_pps_o) MDIO (Clause 22 and Clause 45) master interface for PHY device configuration and management Tx Features Preamble and start of packet data (SFD) insertion Separate 32-bit status for each packet transmitted from the application Automatic CRC and pad generation controllable on a per-packet basis Programmable packet length to support Standard or Jumbo Ethernet packets with up to 16 kB of size Programmable Inter-Packet Gap IEEE 802.3x Flow Control automatic transmission of zero-quanta Pause packet when flow control input transitions from assertion to de-assertion (in full-duplex mode).

1G Ethernet Controller Source MAC Address field insertion/replacement, and VLAN tag insertion/replacement/ deletion in transmitted packets with per-packet or static-global control Insertion, replacement, or deletion of up to two VLAN tags Option to transmit packets with reduced preamble size in full-duplex mode Insert, replace, or delete VLAN tags based on queue/channel. Rx Features Automatic Pad and CRC Stripping options Option to disable Automatic CRC checking Preamble and SFD deletion Separate 112-bit or 128-bit status Programmable watchdog timeout limit Flexible address-filtering modes: Up to 31 additional 48-bit perfect (DA) address filters with masks for each byte Up to 96 additional 48-bit perfect (DA) address filters that can be selected in blocks of 32 and 64 registers Up to 31 48-bit SA address comparison check with masks for each byte 32-bit, 64-bit, 128-bit, or 256-bit Hash filter (optional) for multicast and unicast (DA) addresses Option to pass all multicast-addressed packets Promiscuous mode to pass all packets without any filtering for network monitoring Pass all incoming packets (as per filter) with a status report. Additional packet filtering: VLAN tag-based: Perfect match and Hash-based (optional) filtering. Filtering based on either outer or inner VLAN tag is possible. Layer 3 and Layer 4-based: TCP or UDP over IPv4 or IPv6 VLAN tag-based filtering (extended) with 4, 8, 16, or 32 filter selections IEEE 802.1Q VLAN tag detection with option to delete the VLAN tags in received packets GPIO based wakeup (PHY detects Wake packets and interrupts controller). Optional forwarding of received Pause packets to the application (in full-duplex mode) Optional Receive module for Layer 3/Layer 4 checksum offload for received packets Optional stripping of VLAN Tags and providing the tags in the status.
#### 10.6.1.3 Transaction Layer (MTL)
The Transaction Layer (MTL) block has a 36 KB Tx FIFO and a 36 KB Rx FIFO. Multiple queues (up to eight) share the FIFO space and the buffer size is configurable for each queue in multiples of 256 bytes. The MTL block supports the following features:

1G Ethernet Controller
##### 10.6.1.3.1 Tx and Rx Features
128-bit Transaction Layer block (bridges the application and the MAC) Data transfers executed using simple FIFO protocol. Synchronization for all clocks in the design (Transmit, Receive, and Application clocks) Optimization for packet-oriented transfers with packets delimiters Programmable burst length, up to half the size of the MTL Rx Queue or Tx Queue size, to support burst data transfer in the EQOS-AXI configuration Programmable threshold capability for each queue (default of 64 bytes) Optional debug and slave mode operation on Queue 0 (default queue) Tx Features FIFO sizes on transmission: up to 128 kB Multiple queues (up to eight) on the Transmit path with a common memory for all Tx Queues Store-and-Forward mechanism or threshold mode (cut-through) for transmission to the MAC Programmable queue size in configurations with multiple queues. Each queue size can be programmed in terms of 256 bytes. Automatic retransmission of collision packets in half-duplex mode Discard packets on late collision, excessive collisions, excessive deferral, and under-run conditions with appropriate status. Calculate and insert IPv4 header checksum and TCP, UDP, or ICMP checksum. Programmable interrupt options for different operational conditions Statistics by generating pulses for packets dropped (due to underflow) in the Tx FIFO Optional statistics related to bandwidth consumption by each queue of up to 16 blocks over a 125 µs period Optional packet-level control for: VLAN tag insertion or replacement Ethernet-source address insertion Layer 3/Layer 4 Checksum insertion control One-step timestamp Timestamp control CRC and pad control The following scheduling algorithms in configurations with multiple queues: Strict Priority (SP) (When Audio-Video Bridging is enabled) Credit-based Shaper (CBS) Option to support dropping of Tx Status to improve the Transmit throughput Rx Features Rx Queue sizes in the receive path: up to 128 kB

1G Ethernet Controller Multiple queues (up to eight) on the receive path with a common memory for all Rx Queues Insertion of Rx Status vectors into the Rx Queue after the EOP transfer (in Threshold mode) and before SOP (in Store-and-Forward mode) in EQOS-AXI configuration Programmable Rx Queue threshold (default fixed at 64 bytes) in Threshold (or cut-through) mode Option to filter all error packets on reception and not forward them to the application in the store-and-forward mode. Option to forward the undersized good packets Statistics by generating pulses for packets dropped (due to overflow) in the Rx FIFO Automatic generation of Pause packet control or backpressure signal to the MAC based on the Rx Queue fill level. Arbitration among queues when multiple queues are present. The following arbitration schemes are supported: Weighted Strict priority (WSP) Strict Priority (SP)
#### 10.6.1.4 Direct Memory Access (DMA) Block
The DMA block exchanges data between the MTL block and system memory. The well-defined descriptors structure acts as a software and hardware interface. The application uses a set of registers (DMA CSR) to control the DMA operations. The DMA block supports the following features: Support for a maximum of eight DMA channels 128-bit data transfers Multichannel Transmit and Receive engines (up to eight transmit channels; up to eight receive channels). Separate DMA channel in the Transmit path for each queue in MTL Single or multiple DMA channels for any number of queues in MTL Receive path Fully synchronous design operating on a single application clock (except for CSR module, when a separate CSR clock is configured). Optimization for packet-oriented DMA transfers with packet delimiters. Byte-aligned addressing for data buffer support Dual-buffer (ring) descriptor support Descriptor architecture to permits large blocks of data transfer with minimum CPU intervention (each descriptor can transfer up to 32 KB of data). Comprehensive status reporting for normal operation and transfers with errors. Individual programmable burst length for Tx DMA and Rx DMA engines for optimal host bus utilization Programmable interrupt options for different operational conditions Per-packet Transmit or Receive Complete Interrupt control.

1G Ethernet Controller Round-robin or fixed-priority arbitration between the Receive and Transmit engines Start and Stop modes Separate ports for host CSR access and host data interface Selectable number of Tx DMA channels with TCP Segmentation Offload (TSO) feature enabled Received packets routing to the DMA channels based on the DA or VLAN Priority in multichannel DMA configurations. Header Payload Split: Option to split the packet header (up to Layer 2, Layer 3 and Layer 4) and payload in different buffers Time-sensitive conditional packet transmission by comparing the Slot Time information provided in the descriptor (useful for Audio Video applications)
#### 10.6.1.5 MACsec Media Access Control Security (MACsec) Block
The Ethernet Controller supports the following MACsec features: Supports IEEE 802.1AE_2018 based packet authentication. Packet Encryption is not supported. Supports up to 1G port speed. Only supported in full duplex mode Supports AES-GCM-128 and AES-GCM-256 based ICV generation and checking Only 16 bytes ICV configuration is supported. Thirty-two Secure Association Keys (SAKs) supported in Receive and Transmit direction Maximum number of Secure Channels (SCs) supported is 16 with two Association Number (AN) each. With 4 AN, maximum eight SCs can be supported. Supports 32-bit Packet Number (PN) No supports for 64-bit PN support (Extended PN as defined in IEEE 802.1AEbw-2013). Hardware-based Packet Number (PN) exhaustion check and automatic jump over to next AN, if configured, in transmit direction. Replay Window or strict-order based replay protection Flow-based or global Bypass support Permits uncontrolled port traffic flowing through Ethernet port Statistics and Status for various MACsec related states and counters as defined by IEEE 802.1AE_2018 Support for Preemptible and Express packets as specified in as defined by IEEE 802.1Qbu-2016 Classification based on Flexible Offset Flexible Frame Validation check on Ingress Support for Legacy-Ethernet packets like SNAP, LLC packets Majority of SecY functionality is implemented in hardware.

1G Ethernet Controller Hard Separation of register space for SecY and KaY pages
- SecY manages various MACsec controls like lookup, and so on.
- KaY manages Crypto Keys, Crypto ICVs, and Crypto state control parameters.
Advanced debug support for both Receive and Transmit direction Safety features for Safety Critical applications
##### 10.6.1.5.1 Reduced Gigabit Media Independent Interface (RGMII)
The RGMII module is implemented in DWC_ether_qos to reduce the pin count. The RGMII specification reduces the pin count of the interconnection between the MAC and the PHY for GMII and MII interfaces. To achieve this, the datapath and control signals are reduced and multiplexed together with both edges of the Transmit and Receive clocks. For Gigabit operation, the clocks operate at 125 MHz; for 10/100 operation, the clock rates are 2.5 MHz/25 MHz.
##### 10.6.1.5.2 AXI Interface
AXI interface features can be divided into the following categories: AXI Master Interface Features AXI Slave Interface Features AXI Master Interface Features The AXI master interface supports the following features: Interfaces with the application through AXI4 compatible interface 40-bit address width Little-endian and byte-invariant big-endian modes AXI low-power interface 128-bit datapath OKAY, SLVERR, and DECERR responses Software-selected Type of AXI burst (fixed and variable length burst) in AXI master interface; Extended length-fixed bursts of 32, 64, 128, and 256 supported Address-aligned bursts 4 KB boundary burst splitting and support for limiting burst to 1 KB boundary Up to 32 outstanding Read and Write transactions Posted writes during multiple data transfers from the AXI master interface to maximize the bus use. Handshaking on AXI Read and Write data channels

1G Ethernet Controller AXI Slave Interface Features Does not support Slave Interface. Use 32b wide APB interface to access control and status registers.
##### 10.6.1.5.3 Important Usage Models
Time Sensitive Networking (TSN) The Ethernet Controller supports the following TSN features: Time Synchronization IEEE 1588-2008 for precision-networked clock synchronization IEEE 802.1as-201, timing, and synchronization for time-sensitive applications in bridged LANs IEEE 802.1Qat and IEEE 802.1Qav standards, Virtual Bridged LANs IEEE 1722-2011, Layer 2-transport protocol for time-sensitive apps in bridged LANs IEEE 802.1Qbv-2015 for Enhancements to Scheduling Traffic IEEE802.1Qbu/802.3br for Frame preemption and Interspersing Express Supports MACsec for both Express and Preemptible frames MACsec features are defined in a previous section. AV Support The Ethernet Controller supports the following AV features: Separate channels or queues for AV data transfer in 100 Mbps and 1,000 Mbps modes Up to eight queues on the Receive paths for AV traffic and seven queues on the Transmit path for AV traffic IEEE 802.1-Qav specified credit-based shaper (CBS) algorithm for Transmit channels Single Tx FIFO and Rx FIFO (MTL) for all selected queues (system-side interface [AHB, AXI, or native] remains the same). Monitoring, Testing, and Debugging Support The Ethernet Controller supports the following features for monitoring, testing, and debugging: Internal loop-back from Tx to Rx on the GMII for debugging DMA states (Tx and Rx) as status bits Debug status register that gives status of FSMs in Transmit and Receive datapaths and FIFO fill-levels Application Abort status bits

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description MMC (RMON) module Current Tx or Rx Buffer pointer as status registers Current Tx or Rx Descriptor pointer as status registers Statistical counters to calculate the bandwidth served by each Transmit channel when AV support is enabled Tx or Rx Queues memory accessible through Slave port for debug
#### 10.6.1.6 Features Not Supported
##### 10.6.1.6.1 Frame-Based Arbitration
When operating in either Threshold (cut through) or Store and forward modes of operation, PBL- based arbitration is recommended over Frame based arbitration.
##### 10.6.1.6.2 Ignore Programmable Burst Length
Before placing a request for a data read from memory, the Tx controller checks that entries equivalent to the data request size (which is equal to Tx PBL) are available in the corresponding Tx Queue. If the space is available, it places a request on memory side. But, the IP also supports Ignore Programmable Burst Length (IPBL) in which the DMA does not check for the PBL number of locations in the MTL before initiating a transfer. Therefore, use of IPBL is not recommended.
##### 10.6.1.6.3 Maximum AXI Burst Length of Four with TSO Enabled
The Ethernet Controller can program the burst length supported on AXI from a value of four up to 256 in powers of 2. When TCP Segmentation Offload is enabled, if the AXI burst length is less than the TCP/IP header size, a defect in the IP can cause one of the DMA channels to stop functioning. Because the maximum IPv4 header is 80 Bytes, if the AXI burst is programmed to a value greater than 5, this limitation does not occur since each burst is of 16B. Therefore, when TSO is enabled, the AXI BLEN enabled in the IP must be a minimum of 8 to avoid this issue.
### 10.6.2 1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description
#### 10.6.2.1 Overview
Ether_QOS is the 1G Ethernet Controller that supports 10M/100M/1G line speeds over its RGMII interface. Ether_QOS also supports MACsec. The ETHER_QOS block diagram is shown below. The IP is configured with an AXI4 master interface for system memory access and APB4 slave interfaces for CSR access from the host software.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description
**Figure 10.25 ETHER_QOS Block Diagram**
The 1GMAC DMA controller has eight receive and eight transmit channels. The DMA controller reads data from system memory (through AXI4 master interface) into transmit (Tx) memory buffer. The MTL and MAC blocks manage the transmission of data from the Tx buffer to the network. The data received on the network is stored into receive (Rx) memory buffer of the controller. The Rx DMA controller writes the Rx buffer data to the system memory (through AXI4 master interface). The 1GMAC micro-architecture provides 1GMAC access to six memory buffers: TSO memory: 8 kB of on chip memory to store headers for Transmit Segmentation Offload Tx Memory: 64 kB of on-chip memory to store transmit packets Rx Memory: 64 kB of on-chip memory to store received packets EST memory: 2 kB Memory for Descriptor Cache RXP memory: 3 kB of Receiver Parser memory Descriptor Cache: 4 kB The Ethernet data from 1GMAC is connected to MACSEC IP, which implements MACSEC ICV generation and checking in compliance with IEEE802.1AE. The output of the MACSEC IP is connected to the pads and then reach out off chip PHY. The 1GMAC has multiple interrupts for various events that can occur in its MAC or in its DMA controller. The controller also generates fault

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description signals that is connected to HSM (Hardware Safety Manager) block on the chip to report faults in Ethernet Controller logic.
#### 10.6.2.2 Interfaces
##### 10.6.2.2.1 Internal Interfaces
AXI4 Master Interface The 1GMAC DMA controller issues requests on an AXI4 master interface to access system memory. Table 10.12 ETHER_QOS AXI parameters # Parameter Size AXI Address Width 40 bit AXI Data Width 128 bit AXI Master Bus ID Width 8 bit AXI Maximum Outstanding Read Requests AXI Maximum Outstanding Write Requests AXI Clock Frequency 125 MHz APB4 Slave Interface 1GMAC control interface supports APB4 slave interface. The slave interface uses the Async Slave bridge to ensure that there is no clock dependency with respect to CBB (Control Back Bone) clock for internal functionality. Block Level Firewall logic in Control Backbone provides access protection between Hypervisor, Resource Manager, and Virtual Machine pages. The IP can generate an APB slave error for illegal access based on configuration setting. Interrupt Interface Ether QOS provides seven interrupts, as shown in the following table, for its internal IPs. Table 10.13 ETHER_QOS Consolidated LIC Interrupts Output Description eqos_common_intr_o Common aggregated interrupt of sbd_intr_o, lpi_intr_o, pmt_intr_o, safety interrupts eqos_MACsec_secure_intr Secured interrupt status from MACSEC

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description Output Description eqos_MACsec_non_secure_intr Non-Secured interrupt status from MACSEC eqos_vm_intr_o[3:0] Per VM interrupt pin. Individual TX/RX DMA channel interrupts mapped to VM interrupts HSM Fault Interrupt Interface ETHER_QOS supports multiple safety faults interrupts generated by its internal IPs. These interrupts are consolidated into three fault interrupts and sent to the HSM (Hardware Safety Manager). Table 10.14 ETHER_QOS Consolidated HSM Interrupts Output Description eqos_hsm_correctable_error Consolidated correctable error from ETHER_QOS and ETHER_QOS wrapper modules eqos_hsm_uncorrectable_error Consolidated uncorrectable error from 1GMAC and ETHER_QOS wrapper modules eqos_macsec_hsm_uncorrectable_error Consolidated uncorrectable error from 1GMAC MACsec Timestamp Interface The 1GMAC controller provides various signals shown in the following table to Synchronize TSC Module with received PTP timestamp value. The upper 32 bits of timestamp corresponds to number of seconds and the lower 32 bit corresponds to nanoseconds granularity. Internal timestamp Controller (TSC) logic uses this timestamp to synchronize its internal clock. Table 10.15 Timestamp Interface IP/Wrapper Signal Name Di r Description Usage/Remarks ptp_timestamp_o[ 63:0] Ou t Reference Time Output. This bus provides the System Time Output when it is generated internally. Used to capture the PTP and TSC value simultaneously. ptp_pps_o Ou t Pulse Per Second. This signal is high based on the PPS mode selected in the MAC_PPS_Control register. When PPS is programmed in Media Clock recovery Mode, this port indicates the recovered clock. Sent to TSC. Used by TSC for global reference and correction of TSC time. ptp_aux_ts_trig_i[ 0] In Auxiliary timestamp Trigger. When this signal goes high (rising edge), a snapshot of the System Time is taken and stored in the auxiliary timestamp FIFO. Used to capture the PTP timestamp snapshot in the AUX timestamp FIFO

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description Pad Calibration Interface The RGMII pads in Ether QOS support drive strength compensation. Pad Calibration Logic is used to provide this compensation. Perform a PAD calibration when any of the following conditions occur: Before initializing the EQOS MAC controller. When there is a change in speed from 10 Mbps to either 100 Mbps or 1,000 Mbps. If there is a temperature variation of more than 35 degrees Celsius. Note: Before PAD calibration starts, it is recommended that RGMII and MDIO interfaces are in IDLE state. Any ongoing RGMII traffic must be stopped, otherwise communication errors might occur. The NVIDIA EQOS driver software handles the PAD calibration mechanism, which already takes care of the above-mentioned conditions. Calibration Process Compare the PMOS driving impedance with an external precision resistance of 50 Ω ± 1% lumped to ground. Then use the calibrated PMOS driving impedance as a reference to proceed the calibration of NMOS driving impedance. As shown in following diagram, input A is first set to ‘1’ to charge the pad I/O while NMOS driver is deactivated. The number of PMOS fingers is turned on sequentially by increasing the DRVUP codes to raise the total current flowing through the resistor. The resulting I*R at I/O is then compared with a 0.5*VDDP reference. When I/O reaches 0.5*VDDP, ZI turns into ‘1’ and the PMOS calibration ends. Similarly, for NMOS calibration, A is being set to ‘0’ to discharge I/O with partially turned on PMOS fingers based on the DRVUP codes obtained in PMOS calibration. By gradually increasing the DRVDN codes (hence the number of NMOS fingers) IO_N drops and finally ZI flips to ‘0’ when IO_N reaches 0.5*VDDP. This completes the calibration process.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description
**Figure 10.26 Calibration Process**
Calibration Controller The calibration controller is implemented as per the above-mentioned process. The calibration controller uses ‘usec_toggle’ pulse sourced from TIMER module. It toggles for every micro-second, which is used as micro-second reference in maintaining the micro-second counter in calibration engine. The FSM implementation is shown in the following diagram.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description
**Figure 10.27 Calibration Controller**
##### 10.6.2.2.2 External Interfaces
The Ether QOS pad logic can support 1.8 V operation. The interface constitutes 16 pins (RGMII Interface: 12 pins, MDIO Interface: 2 pins, GPIO Interface: 2 pins). Both INTR and RESET are GPIO only. The PMC handles the INTR pin. The INTR pin is wake capable. RGMII RGMII has 12 pin interfaces; 6 are related to TX and other 6 are related to RX interface. The interface operates in DDR mode. This interface supports the Original RGMII Timing mode though the PHY/Switch component interfacing with ETHER_QOS must support RGMII-ID timing mode to avoid Clock Delay in relation to the data on the PCB. The data rates of this interface are 10/100/1000Mbps at 2.5/25/125 MHz respectively with a 4-bit data interface at DDR speeds simultaneously for both Tx and Rx transfers.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description MDIO This is a 2-signal interface to PHY to access the PHY control and status registers. The interface constitutes a clock line at 2.5 MHz from the SoC to the PHY and the other line is a bidirectional data line. The MDC Clock line can support frequencies from 2.5 MHz to 25 MHz. The ETHER_QOS acts as the master to this interface. INTR by External PHY This signal is used by the external PHY to communicate to the SoC for its internally generated interrupts--that requires the attention of the software. Then software uses the MDIO interface to access the PHY control and status registers to service the interrupts. RESET to External PHY The RESET pin to external Ethernet PHY, which is a GPIO pin, is used to reset the external PHY.. The software controls the RESET pin. As part of the PHY initialization sequence, the RESET pin GPIO is programmed to apply the reset to external PHY and to recover from errors. It is an active low signal driven from the GPIO controller module.
#### 10.6.2.3 Features
##### 10.6.2.3.1 Power Management
Wake On LAN The Ether QOS supports GPIO-based remote wake-up function. Attached PHY, on receiving the Wake Up packet can generate Wake up trigger signal on connected GPIO. The PMC uses it to wake up the Ethernet Controller. Energy-Efficient Ethernet The (EEE) mode is compliant with the IEEE 802.3az-2010 standard. It is primarily targeted to save power in the Ethernet port when there is no traffic on the line. In this mode, the host indicates to the far-end that it does not have any packets to transmit for the near future. The host puts the transmitter port (MAC Controller, SERDES, and attached PHY) into low-power mode. Similarly, the receiver port can also be put into low-power mode when the far-end host indicates that it does not have any traffic to transfer. This gives significant saving of power in the Ethernet port (mainly in the PHY) with intermittent and bursty traffic profile. The triggering of entry and exit out of the EEE mode is controlled by the MAC and is supported within the Ether QOS. Simultaneous operation of the EEE mode along with any or both the other power-saving modes is also supported in DWC_ether_qos.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description Packet Filtering The following figure shows the packet-filtering sequence on received packets.
**Figure 10.28 Packet Filtering Sequence**
The preceding filtering sequence is valid when all the filters (L2, VLAN, L3, L4) are active. If any of the layer filters are not enabled, that filter is bypassed and the subsequent filter is applied. A packet that fails any of the filters is discarded. However, the discarded packet can be forwarded to the host based on the register control. For example, when Bit RA of MAC_Packet_Filter register is set to 1, all discarded packets are forwarded to the host but with its packet status indicating the specific filter failure. Ethernet Source or Destination Address Filters The filters support various kinds of Ethernet Source and Destination address-based filtering operations. Some of them are defined: Unicast Destination Address based filtering: Both perfect and hash filter-based checks are provided on up to 128 MAC Addresses. Multicast Destination Address Filtering: The multicast address is compared with the programmed MAC destination address registers (1–31).

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description Broadcast Address filtering: The MAC does not filter any broadcast packets by default. To program the MAC to reject all broadcast packets, set the DBF bit in MAC_Packet_Filter register. Unicast Source Address Filtering: The MAC can perform perfect filtering based on the source address field of received packets. Inverse Filtering: For DA and SA filtering, the filter-match result at the final output can be inverted. VLAN Filters In VLAN tag perfect filtering, the MAC compares the VLAN tag of received packet and provides the VLAN packet status to the application. The source or destination address (if enabled) has precedence over the VLAN tag filters. This means that a packet that fails the source or destination address filter is dropped irrespective of the VLAN tag filter results. The MAC Receiver can classify the received packets based on VLAN Tag and steer them to a specific Rx DMA channel. Each of the VLAN Tags has individual control over stripping. The programming options of always strip, never strip, strip on pass, and strip on fail are available. Inner or Outer VLAN tag stripping is based on the pass or fail results of the individual tag. IP Source or Destination Address Filters The DWC_ether_qos supports perfect matching or inverse matching for IP source address and destination address. In addition, you can match the complete IP address or mask the lower bits matching, that is, compare all bits of the address except the specified lower mask bits. TCP or UDP Source or Destination Port Filters The DWC_ether_qos supports perfect matching or inverse matching for TCP or UDP Source and Destination Port numbers.
##### 10.6.2.3.2 Using PHY Interfaces
The main PHY interfaces are described in the following sections. Station Management Agent (SMA) The application can access the PHY registers through the SMA. The SMA is a two-wire Station Management interface (MIM). Preamble Suppression The IEEE standard specifies 32-bit preamble (all-ones) for the MDIO frames. The DWC_ether_qos provides controls to support preamble suppression. DWC_ether_qos transmits MDIO frames with

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description only one preamble bit. The preamble suppression can be enabled by setting the PSE bit of the MAC_MDIO_Address register. MDIO Transaction completion Interrupt DWC_ether_qos can generate an interrupt on completion of MDIO read or write transactions. Therefore, the application does not need to poll the GMII Busy field of the MAC_MDIO_Address register to know the completion of MDIO commands. RGMII (Reduced Gigabit Media Independent) Interface The RGMII Interface to the Physical Layer is capable of working at 1Gb/s, 100Mb/s and 10Mb/s. It supports MACsec when the link is operating at 1 Gbps speed. MACsec is not supported for 10 Mbps and 100 Mbps operations. The RGMII module is implemented in DWC_ether_qos to reduce the pin count as mentioned in the RGMII specification. The RGMII specification reduces the pin count of the interconnection between the MAC and the PHY for GMII and MII interfaces. To achieve this, the datapath and control signals are reduced and multiplexed together with both edges of the Transmit and Receive clocks. For Gigabit operation, the clocks operate at 125 MHz; for 10/100 operation, the clock rates are 2.5 MHz/25 MHz. The RGMII module is instantiated between the GMII of the MAC and the PHY to translate the control and data signals between the GMII and RGMII protocols. The RGMII block has the following characteristics: Supports 10 Mbps, 100 Mbps, and 1,000 Mbps operation rates Requires no extra clock because both edges of the incoming clocks are used for 1 Gbps operation though for 10/100 Mbps operation, only a single clock edge is used. Extracts the in-band (link speed, link status, and duplex mode) status signals from the PHY and provides them to the MAC for link detection. The following figure shows the position of the RGMII block relative to the MAC and RGMII PHY. The RGMII block is placed between the GMII and the PHY to translate the GMII signals to RGMII signals.
**Figure 10.29 RGMII Interface**

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description
**Figure 10.30 RGMII Interface Pinout Diagram**
##### 10.6.2.3.3 IEEE 1588 Timestamp Support
The DWC_ether_qos supports the IEEE 1588-2002 (version 1) and IEEE 1588-2008 (version 2). The IEEE 1588-2002 supports PTP transported over UDP/IP and IEEE 1588-2008 supports PTP transported over Ethernet. The DWC_ether_qos provides programmable support for both standards. The controller supports the following features: Provides an option to take snapshot of all packets or only PTP type packets. Provides an option to take the snapshot based on the clock type: ordinary, boundary, end-to- end transparent, and peer-to-peer transparent. Provides an option to select the node to be a master or slave for ordinary and boundary clock. Identifies the PTP message type, version, and PTP payload in packets sent directly over Ethernet and sends the status. Provides an option to measure sub-second time in digital or binary format. Supports both one-step and two-step PTP Timestamping. Provides the flexibility to program the start or stop time, width, and interval of the pulse generated on the ptp_pps_o output. Provides capability to generate PTP Ethernet messages periodically or from the application, or based on reception of a particular PTP message.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description
##### 10.6.2.3.4 Multiple Channels and Queues
The DWC_ether_qos supports up to eight queues and channels on the Tx and Rx paths. The following figure shows the architecture of DWC_ether_qos with multiple queues and channels. In half duplex configuration (applicable for 10/100M mode), only Q0/Ch0 should be enabled In full duplex operation, any queue/s can be enabled. Tx queue and Rx queue should be 2 * maximum packet size.
**Figure 10.31 DWC_ether_QOS Architecture**
In the Transmit direction, the DWC_ether_qos supports up to eight Transmit DMA and Transmit queues. The number of Tx DMA channels is equal to the number of Tx queues, and is a direct one- to-one mapping. This enables the interleaving of packet/data transfer of multiple Tx DMA on the host/system bus and each Tx queue is reserved for the corresponding Tx DMA. Therefore, the integrity of packet transfer by each Tx DMA is maintained in the Tx queue. The Tx queue enables efficient utilization of the host bus for data transfers among multiple Tx DMA without depending on the packet length, Transmit buffer availability and so on.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description In the receive direction, the DWC_ether_qos controller provides multiple Rx queues to support classification and distribution of ingress packets. The MAC receiver pushes the ingress packets to the Rx queues based on packet type (tagged, untagged, multicast, PTP, AVB, DCB, and so on), tag priorities, MAC packet filter results, preemptable, or express packet, and so on. The settings of the MAC_RxQ_Ctrl* and MAC_Packet_Filter register fields control the distribution. Any of the Rx DMA can service the packets from any Rx queue . All the packets of Rx queues are stored in a shared RXFIFO buffer in MTL. The Rx scheduler selects the Rx queue whose packet data is to be transferred to the destination Rx DMA, which then forwards the packet data to the host memory. The DWC_ether_qos DMA arbiter supports two types of arbitration: fixed priority and weighted round-robin. The DMA arbiter performs the arbitration between the Tx and Rx paths of DMA channels for accessing descriptors and data buffers. The DA bit of the DMA_Mode register specifies the arbitration scheme (fixed or weighted round-robin) between the Tx and Rx DMA of a channel.
##### 10.6.2.3.5 Traffic Shapers
Queue Modes and Priorities Transmit queues can be divided into generic, DCB, and AV traffic types. Generic queues are serviced in WRR (Weighted Round Robin) or WSP (Weighted Strict Priority) order. DCB queues are serviced in WRR, WSP, DWRR, WFQ order. AV queues are serviced using CBS (Credit-Based Shaper) or SP (Strict Priority). The priority of a Tx queue can be programmed in the MAC_TxQ_Prty_Map0 and MAC_TxQ_Prty_Map1 registers. Similarly, the priority of an Rx queue can be programmed in the corresponding field of MAC_RxQ_Ctrl2 and MAC_RxQ_Ctrl3 registers. The priority should be assigned in the following order: 1. 2. 3. AV queue (high priority) DCB queue (medium priority) Best-effort queue (low priority) The software should put packets with correct priorities in the respective programmed queue on Tx side. The MAC uses the programmed priorities for blocking the Tx queues when a PFC packet is received. If a single queue is selected for multiple priorities and PFC is enabled, the entire queue is paused if one or more priorities in the queue are paused. Further details on DCB queues and AV queues are provided in the following sections. Data Center Bridging The Data Center Bridging feature supports three types of algorithms.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description Weighted Round Robin: In this mode, all queues are serviced in round-robin order based on weight setting. Deficit Weighted Round Robin: In this mode, queues are assigned a weight based on the percentage of configured bandwidth. A deficit counter holds the credit for transmission. Weighted Fair Queuing: In this mode, each queue is assigned a weight based on the percentage of the configured bandwidth. The controller schedules the packet with the fastest finish time to start transmission first. Queues assigned to operate in DCB mode are scheduled using the defined algorithms. These queues are also capable of supporting PFC-based flow control. Audio Video Bridging The DWC_ether_qos supports the AV data transfer in 100 Mbps and 1,000 Mbps modes. The AV feature enables transmission of time-sensitive traffic over bridged local area networks (LANs). The following standards define various aspects of the AV feature implementation: IEEE 802.1Qav-2009: Supports forwarding and Queuing for Time-Sensitive Streams. IEEE 802.1Qat-2009: Permits the network resources to be reserved for specific traffic streams traversing a bridged local area network. IEEE 802.1AS-2011: Specifies the protocol and procedures used to ensure that the synchronization requirements are met for time-sensitive applications. Queues assigned to operate in AV mode, support CBS (Credit-Based Shaper as specified in IEEE 802.1-Qav), or SP scheduling algorithms.
##### 10.6.2.3.6 Time Sensitive Networking
There are many applications that require predictable network latency. Some of these applications include audio and video, initially defined in Audio Video Bridging (AVB) standards, automotive sensor control networks as well as advanced driver assistance. To support tight time tolerance as well as predictable network latency requirements of these applications, the Ether QOS implements the following features in hardware. Enhancements to Scheduled Traffic (EST) as defined in IEEE 802.1Qbv Frame preemption and Interspersing Express Traffic as defined in IEEE 802.1Qbu and IEEE 802.3br Time-Based Scheduling to enable above defined features Enhancements to Scheduled Traffic The IEEE 802.1Qbv-2015 defines the schedule for each of the queues on every egress port, which makes the implementation aware of traffic arrival schedule. This information can be used to block the lower priority traffic from transmission in this time window/slot. This ensures that scheduled

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description traffic is forwarded from sender to receiver through all the network nodes with a deterministic delay. This behavior is shown in the following figure.
**Figure 10.32 Scheduled Traffic**
As per the standard, the following updates are needed in the Transmit Scheduler to support EST. Implementation of Gate Control List (GCL) Enforcing gate controls in the scheduler Accounting for Gate Open (O) duty cycle in the computation of idleSlope (CBS) The controller supports all 3 of these requirements in hardware. When EST is used in isolation, the Gate Control List manages the final open/close state of the Queues along with the checks carried out by the Transmission Selection Algorithm in MTL. As the Gate Controls operate on a predefined repetitive schedule, it is recommended to use Strict Priority or Credit Based Shaper (CBS) scheduling algorithms. Frame preemption and Interspersing Express Traffic Preemption permits one or more higher priority (express) frames to interrupt the transmission of a lower priority (preemptable) frame; the preemptable frame transmission is resumed and completed after the express frame transmission is complete. To support frame preemption, the following two abstractions of the MAC are used: A preemptable MAC, called pMAC, which carries the preemptable traffic. An express MAC, called eMAC, which carries the express traffic. pMAC and eMAC operate in parallel as shown in the following figure.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description
**Figure 10.33 Preemptable and Express Traffic**
In the implementation, only parts of the MAC that hold the state during preemption is replicated and represented as pMAC and eMAC. The MAC uses the following two ways to puts on hold, the transmission of the preemtable traffic, in the presence of express traffic: The MTL scheduler interrupts the preemptable traffic that is currently being transmitted. When the preemption capability is active, the MAC interrupts the transmission and reception of preemptable frames. Zero or more express frames follow a preempted fragment, before the continuation fragments. The preemptable frame can be fragmented any number of times, however, the minimum final and nonfinal fragment length criterion must be is met. However, interleaving of more than one preemptable packet is not permitted. This implies that if an express packet fragments a preemptable packet, another preemptable packet cannot be transferred until all the remaining fragments of the first preempted packet are transferred. The MTL scheduler prevents starting the transmission of preemptable traffic. When the preemption capability is inactive, the pMAC entity is disabled and only express traffic is transmitted or received. Frame preemption feature can be enabled by setting EFPE field of the MAC_FPE_CTRL_STS register. Time-Based Scheduling To support the strict transmit time requirements of EST, the controller adds a Time-Based Scheduling feature. In this feature, the transmit DMA fetches the packet from the host memory for transmission at a designated time. This helps the software to set up the Transmit descriptors in advance even before the packet is ready/available. The following “Time” parameters control the queue behavior and enable the controller to adhere to strict time requirements of EST: Launch Time: The time beyond which MTL can schedule the packet for transmission.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description Fetch Time: The time beyond which the Tx DMA can schedule a packet-fetch from the host memory. Expiry Time: The time beyond which the MTL drops the packet. The Time-Based Scheduler does not directly influence the Transmission Selection Algorithm but has an indirect influence as it determines if a queue is eligible to participate in the scheduling. If a frame of a specific queue has a valid Launch Time, the Time-Based Scheduler ensures that the frame participates in Transmit Scheduling (TRC Scheduler) only after the Launch time has elapsed. TCP/IP Offload Features Communication protocols such as TCP and UDP implement checksum fields, which help determine the integrity of data transmitted over a network. The most widespread use of Ethernet is to encapsulate TCP and UDP over IP datagrams. Therefore, the MAC has an optional Checksum Offload Engine (COE) to support checksum calculation and insertion in the transmit path and error detection in the receive path. Details on various offload features provided in the controller are explained in the following sections. Transmit Checksum Offload Engine The MAC has a Checksum Offload Engine (COE) to support checksum calculation and insertion in the Transmit path, using which, the software offloads the task of checksum insertion to the hardware. In the Transmit path MAC calculates the checksum and inserts it in the Tx packet. This feature helps to reduce the load on the software and can improve the overall throughput of the system. The Checksum Offload Engine (COE) supports the following checksum offloads on the transmit path. IPv4 Checksum Offload TCP/UDP/ICMP checksum offload (not true for IPv4 fragment) The L3/L4 checksum can be controlled for each packet using the following options: CIC bits (Transmit Descriptor TDES3 Bits[17:16]). Software needs to program these bits to have checksum generation and insertion in Tx frame. Checksum insertion is enabled for tunneled packets when VNE bit of MAC_Tx_Configuration register is set and the VNP=3’b011 in the Tx Descriptor of the corresponding packet. Setting TSC bit of MAC_Timestamp_Control: This bit enables checksum correction during OST for PTP over UDP/IPv4 packets. Software needs to set this bit to keep the UDP checksum correct for changes made to origin timestamp and/or correction field as part of one-step timestamp operation. This bit is only applicable for PTP packets.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description Receive Checksum Offload Engine Similar to the Transmit Checksum Offload engine, the Receive Checksum Offload Engine detects the following checksum errors. IPv4 Checksum Offload: TCP/UDP/ICMP checksum offload (not true for IPv4 fragment) The Receive Checksum Offload can be controlled for each packet using the following options: Receive Checksum Offload can be enabled by setting IPC bit in MAC_Rx_Configuration register. TCP/IP Checksum Error packet drop control: Setting MTL_RxQ(i=0:9)_Operation_Mode.DIS_TCP_EF bit disables dropping of checksum error packets on Receive. When DIS_TCP_EF bit is set, the MAC does not drop the packets, which only have the errors detected by the Receive Checksum Offload engine. Checksum verification for different types of tunneled packets can be controlled as well using provided register controls. The software can enable/disable checksum error-related interrupts from MMC Counters through MMC_IPC_Rx_Interrupt_Mask register. By default, all interrupts are enabled. TCP/IP Segmentation Offload (TSO) Engine In the TCP segmentation offload (TSO) feature, the DMA splits a large TCP packet into multiple small packets and passes these packets to the MTL as shown in the following figure.
**Figure 10.34 TCP Segmentation Offload Overview**
The TSO operation flow is explained in the following figure.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description
**Figure 10.35 TSO Operation Flow**
The application must create the header in Buffer 1 of the first descriptor of the packet to be segmented and provide the header length in TDES2 of the first descriptor (FD = 1). When the FD bit is set, the DMA reads the header from the header buffer to which the TDES0 is pointing. Buffer 2 of the first descriptor can be used for payload and TDES0 and TDES1 of subsequent descriptors.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description For subsequent descriptors (FD = 0), the address to which the TDES0 and TDES1 are pointing is treated as payload buffer address of the same packet.
**Figure 10.36 Head and Payload Fields of Segmented Packets**
UDP/IPv4 Fragment Offload (UFO) Engine The UFO breaks down a large UDP packet into smaller packets using IPv4 fragmentation. Each IPv4 fragment contains the following header or payload information: Ethernet Header IP Header UDP Header (only in the first fragment) UDP Payload In this mode, the MSS field in the context Descriptor (TDES2[17:0]) and DMA_CH(#)_Control register, are interpreted as Maximum Fragmentation Size (MFS). This is the maximum size of the payload after the IPv4 header in each fragment. When UFO is enabled, the MSS field must be programmed in multiples of 8 bytes, because, the IP fragments offset is defined in terms of 8 bytes. UFO functions in two modes. UFO with valid UDP checksum UFO with no UDP checksum Using the IPv4 ARP Offload Engine DWC_ether_qos supports the Address Recognition Protocol (ARP) Offload for IPv4 packets. This feature allows the processing of the IPv4 ARP request packet in the receive path and generating corresponding ARP response packet in the transmit path. DWC_ether_qos generates the ARP reply packets for appropriate ARP request packets. The ARP packet for IPv4 is L2 layer packet with Length/Type of 0x0806.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description
##### 10.6.2.3.7 Flow Control
Enabling Flow Controls The flow control in the Tx and Rx directions can be enabled using the following controls. To enable the Transmit Flow Control independently for each Rx queue, set the TFE bit in the MAC_Q#_Tx_Flow_Ctrl register. To enable the Pause Flow Control, set the RFE bit in the MAC_Rx_Flow_Ctrl register. Full Duplex Mode In full-duplex mode, the DWC_ether_qos uses one of the following packet types for flow control: IEEE 802.3x Pause packets Priority flow control (PFC) packets The PFC packets are used only when the Enable Data Center Bridging option is selected. The PFCE bit of MAC_Rx_Flow_Ctrl register determines whether the PFC packets or the IEEE 802.3x Pause Control packets are used for flow control. If the PFCE bit is set, the MAC sends the PFC packets. Half Duplex Mode In half-duplex mode, the MAC uses the deferral mechanism for the flow control (back pressure). When the application requests to stop receiving packets, the MAC sends a JAM pattern of 32 bytes when it senses a packet reception, provided the transmit flow control is enabled. This results in a collision and the remote station back off. If the application requests a packet to be transmitted, it is scheduled and transmitted even when the back pressure is activated. If the back pressure is kept activated for a long time (and more than 16 consecutive collision events occur), the remote stations abort the transmission because of excessive collisions. Virtualization The Ethernet Controller supports hardware-assisted virtualization (multiple operating systems share underlying hardware). Hypervisor is responsible to allocate queues and channels to different VMs. The Resource Manager (RM) or one trusted OS programs the common registers shared by multiple VMs. The host accesses controller registers over the APB bus. Each VM is allocated a 64 kB address window in this interface for it to program its registers. Similarly, the RM is provided a separate 64 kB register window to program common registers. A given VM only has access to the registers allocated to it and cannot access another VMs register space. Registers Address Space The following figure shows the address map of ETHER_QOS. The figure shows how the register space is mapped to various VMs, RM, and HV. They are physically aliased at 64 KB to enable easy mapping in the host MMU. VMs have access and visibility to only a register space marked in blue.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description Access to these spaces by specific VMs are controlled by the RM by configurating appropriate mapping register in the ETHER_QOS. Other register spaces are only assigned to the RM. The RM can also access all the registers that are accessible by VMs.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description
**Figure 10.37 Address Map of ETHER_QOS**

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description The following register access operations are considered illegal operations: One Guest OS trying to access other Guest OS registers Any Guest OS trying to access registers belonging to RM or HV page. RM trying to access registers in HV page HV trying to access registers in RM or any Guest OS page. The Guest OS illegal access status is captured in the following register: ETHER_QOS_VIRTUAL_APB_ERR_STATUS_0 The option to generate APB slave error for guest OS illegal access can be enabled by programming the following register: ETHER_QOS_VIRTUAL_APB_ERR_CTRL_0 Similarly, RM or HV illegal access status is captured in the following register: ETHER_QOS_HV_APB_ERR_STATUS_0 The option to generate an APB slave error for RM or HV illegal access can be enabled by programming the following register: ETHER_QOS_HV_APB_ERR_CTRL_0 The ETHER_QOS can support up to maximum of four guest OSes, 1 RM, and 1 HV. Therefore, six 64 KB pages [4 VMs and 1RM and 1HV] of address space is needed. The RM page should have access to a whole region. If virtualization is not employed, the [only] operating system could operate in the HV/RM register window directly. The implementation is shown below.

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description
**Figure 10.38 Register Windows Design**
PTP Register Access from VMs The PTP registers require common read access by all VMs. Therefore, these registers are placed in a separate 64 kB address window, which is accessible by all VMs. ETHER_QOS VM5 AMAP page is used for this purpose. System Memory Protection mechanism for Ether QOS Controller Since the DMA controller of the Ether QOS generates memory requests on AXI using AXI_ID[3:1], which is based on issuing channel number, a conversion table is provided at the interface to convert AXI_ID[3:1] to ASID (address space identifier for different VMs in the Ethernet Controller) used by the SMMU. Hypervisor programs the conversions table before the Controller’s VMs issues access to system memory. Generally, a guest OS memory space is protected by the CPU’s MMU (for CPU-generated requests) or by the MC’s SMMU (for non-CPU generated requests). 1GMAC’s DMA controller makes requests directly to system memory over its AXI interface. Assuming 1GMAC is performing DMA on behalf of multiple guest OSes; each memory request has

1G Ethernet Controller Functional Description to be annotated with the correct ASID (address space identifier) to enable SMMU to determine whether 1GMAC can perform the desired operation. The AXI ID [3:1] issued on the AXI master interface corresponds to the DMA channel number associated with the request. A mapping table converts AXI ID [3:1] to ASID. The mapping table is mapped to 64 KB HV page. The reset value of ASIDs is 0. Interrupt Management Ether QOS provides per VM interrupt besides providing a common interrupt that provides common interrupt status. The following figure shows how these interrupts are wired to LIC.
**Figure 10.39 Interrupt Management**

1G Ethernet Controller Programming Guidelines Descriptor Prefetch The Ether QOS supports a descriptor cache. When the descriptor cache operation is enabled, the DMA uses the memory for transmit and receive descriptor cache. Each Tx/Rx DMA channel can cache multiple descriptors based on the values of the following parameters: DWC_EQOS_DCTX_DEP: The value of this parameter determines the number of descriptors that can be fetched for every Tx DMA. The maximum value is 16. DWC_EQOS_DCRX_DEP: The value of this parameter determines the number of descriptors that can be fetched for every Rx DMA. The maximum value is 16.
### 10.6.3 1G Ethernet Controller Programming Guidelines
#### 10.6.3.1 Virtualization Programming Guidelines
The Virtualization register programming is the first step before exercising any other feature of the ETHER_QOS IP.
##### 10.6.3.1.1 Address Range
ETHER_QOS has 10x64KB of address space allocated consecutively. ETHER_QOS_HV address space is allocated to HV. ETHER_QOS_RM address space is allocated to RM. Any CPU that accesses ETHER_QOS through the ETHER_QOS_RM (64KB) address space is treated as RM. ETHER_QOS Sub Apertures Reserved/ In use Offset from Base Addr NV_ADDRESS_MAP_EQOS_BASE ETHER_MAC_HV In use 0x00000 ETHER_MAC_RM In use 0x10000 ETHER_MAC_VM0 In use 0x20000 ETHER_MAC_VM1 In use 0x30000 ETHER_MAC_VM2 In use 0x40000 ETHER_MAC_VM3 In use 0x50000 ETHER_MAC_VM4 Reserved 0x60000 ETHER_MAC_VM5 (Used to access only PTP registers) In use 0x70000

1G Ethernet Controller Programming Guidelines ETHER_QOS Sub Apertures Reserved/ In use Offset from Base Addr NV_ADDRESS_MAP_EQOS_BASE ETHER_MAC_VM6 Reserved 0x80000 ETHER_MAC_VM7 Reserved 0x90000
##### 10.6.3.1.2 Registers Access Control
RM is a trusted software and has unrestricted access for write and read of both core and wrapper registers other than HV page registers. For Guest OSes Core registers: Read access is provided for all registers except the unassigned DMA channel registers and Read_to_Clear (RC) registers. Write access is provided to only the DMA channel registers that are allocated for that particular Guest OS Wrapper registers: Write and Read access is only provided to the respective ETHER_QOS_VIRTUAL_INTR_CHx registers that RM configures.
##### 10.6.3.1.3 Allocation of Channels (CHx)
1GMAC has eight CHx that support both Write (write to Ethernet network) and Read (read from Ethernet network) capability. A single CHx should be allocated to, at most, one Guest OS by RM. Note: Half-duplex mode only CH0 can be used on Tx Side. On the Rx side, multiple queues and channels can be enabled. The Hypervisor can allocate ownership of DMA channels to Guest OSes by programming the VIRTUAL_APB_CHx_DMA_CTRL registers.
##### 10.6.3.1.4 Illegal Registers Access
The ETHER_QOS IP generates an error signal if there is an illegal register access. If a Guest OS tries to access the CHx registers that is assigned to other Guest OSes, then it is treated as a security issue and hence these are treated as errors. The slave error is generated when the corresponding guest OS control bit is enabled in VIRTUAL_APB_ERR_CTRL, which RM can only access. During illegal register access, all writes to registers are dropped and all register reads are masked by returning the value zero.

1G Ethernet Controller Programming Guidelines
##### 10.6.3.1.5 Assigning Address Stream ID for all channels on AXI/Memory Interface
Through VIRTUAL_AXI_ASIDx_CTRL register programming, only the Hypervisor can assign different address stream IDs for different channels.
#### 10.6.3.2 Guidelines to Access PTP Registers from VMs
PTP Registers are from offset 0xb00 to 0xbff. Any VM can read these registers through ETHER_QOS VM5 AMAP page. All VMs, which require PTP register read access, can issue the read transactions with the base address: NV_ADDRESS_MAP_EQOS_MAC_VM5_BASE. Hardware issues a slave error for any other read or write transactions to ETHER_QOS VM5 AMAP page.
#### 10.6.3.3 Guidelines for Handling ETHER_QOS_VM[i]_interrupt by Guest
OS 1. RM sets up DMA to VM mapping by programming the following registers: ETHER_QOS_VIRTUAL_APB_CHx_DMA_CTRL_0 TX and RX DMA channel interrupts capture is enabled by programming the following registers. ETHER_QOS_VIRTUAL_INTR_CHx_CTRL_0 DMA channel interrupts are captured in per channel interrupt status registers. ETHER_QOS_VIRTUAL_INTR_CHx_STATUS_0 Interrupts for all DMA channels are also captured in the following global register as Read only bits. ETHER_QOS_VIRTUAL_INTR_DMA_GLOBAL_STATUS_0 Tx and Rx DMA channel interrupts are mapped to eqos_vm_intr [3:0] based on the DMA Channel to VM-mapping registers. When VM receives interrupt, it should carry out the following operation: 2. 3. 4. 5. 6. a. b. Read ETHER_QOS_VIRTUAL_INTR_DMA_GLOBAL_STATUS_0 Handle the interrupt in the 1GMAC core logic as per the “Interrupts” in the following section. Clear interrupt by writing to the corresponding interrupt bits in ETHER_QOS_VIRTUAL_INTR_CHx_STATUS_0 c. i. Clearing of channel interrupt status clears the corresponding bit in global status register too.
##### 10.6.3.3.1 Interrupts
Interrupts can be generated as a result of various events in the DWC_ether_qos controller. These events are captured in status registers. Interrupt enables are provided for each source of an interrupt such that the interrupt signal (sbd_intr_o) is asserted for an event only when the corresponding interrupt enable is set. In EQOS-AXI configuration, the interrupt status and

1G Ethernet Controller Programming Guidelines corresponding enable registers are organized in a hierarchical manner so that it is easier for software to traverse and identify the source of an interrupt event quickly. When sbd_intr_o is asserted, the DMA_Interrupt_Status register is the first level that indicates the major blocks for the interrupt event source. This register is read-only, and it contains bits corresponding to each DMA channel (TX and RX pair), the MTL, and the MAC. The software application must then read one (or more) of the following registers corresponding to the bits that are set: MAC_Interrupt_Status register MTL_Interrupt_Status register DMA_CH(#i)_Status (for i = 0; i <= DWC_EQOS_NUM_DMA_TX_CH-1) register
#### 10.6.3.4 Guidelines for Handling EQOS_common_intr
1. Read EQOS_COMMON_INTR_STATUS register to know the root cause of the interrupt. It can be any of the following: Correctable error from 1GMAC Core Uncorrectable error from 1GMAC Core SBD Interrupt from 1GMAC Core LPI Interrupt from 1GMAC Core PMT Interrupt from 1GMAC Core Register Parity Error from ETHER_QOS Wrapper Registers 2. Read ETHER_QOS_COMMON_INTR_ENABLE_0 register to know which of the preceding errors are propagated on the common interrupt line. If the interrupt is due to: 3. a. SBD interrupt from 1GMAC Core i. Refer to the “Interrupts” section above. Write 1 to clear SBD Intr status in EQOS_COMMON_INTR_STATUS register. ii. b. LPI interrupt or PMT interrupt from 1GMAC Core i. Refer to the "LPI Interrupt" in the following section. Write 1 to clear the corresponding status in EQOS_COMMON_INTR_STATUS register. ii. c. Register Parity Error from ETHER_QOS Wrapper Registers i. This error occurs when the last read register value has some corrupt data. Error recovery can be done in either of the following ways: ii. a. Writing into that register again, clear the status in EQOS_COMMON_INTR_STATUS register and checking if the parity error goes away. Resetting the IP b. d. Correctable error or uncorrectable error from 1GMAC Core i. Refer to the "Interrupt for Parity Error" the following section. Write 1 to clear the corresponding bits in EQOS_COMMON_INTR_STATUS register. ii.

1G Ethernet Controller Programming Guidelines
##### 10.6.3.4.1 Interrupt for Parity Error
DWC_ether_qos generates an uncorrectable interrupt, sbd_sfty_ue_intr_o to indicate to the application if any parity error is detected. Appropriate status is indicated in DMA/ MTL_Safety_Interrupt_Status and MAC_DPP_FSM_Interrupt_Status registers. All the parity errors reported by the different checkers are logged in the MAC_DPP_FSM_Interrupt_Status register. Note: A parity error is uncorrectable, and in most cases the operation of the DWC_ether_qos is not guaranteed after a parity error. A software reset (for DMA and higher configurations) or a hardware reset (for MTL configuration) is required to recover safely from the parity error reported by the assertion of sbd_sfty_ue_intr_o signal.
##### 10.6.3.4.2 LPI Interrupt
The MAC generates the LPI interrupt when the Tx or Rx side enters or exits the LPI state. The interrupt mci_intr_o (sbd_intr_o in EQOS-DMA configurations) is asserted when the LPI interrupt status is set. The LPI interrupt can be cleared by reading the MAC_LPI_Control_Status register. When the MAC exits the Rx Low Power Interrupt (LPI) state, then in addition to the mci_intr_o (sbd_intr_o in EQOS-DMA configurations), the sideband signal lpi_intr_o (synchronous to Rx clock) is asserted. You can use the lpi_intr_o signal to trigger the external clock-gating circuitry to restore the application clock to the MAC. The lpi_intr_o signal, synchronous to the Rx clock domain, is provided so that you can stop the application clock when the MAC is in the LPI state. If you do not want to gate-off the application clock during the Rx LPI state, you can leave the lpi_intr_o signal unconnected. Then, use the mci_intr_o (sbd_intr_o in EQOSDMA configurations) signal to detect Rx LPI exit. The lpi_intr_o signal is generated in the Rx clock domain. It may not be cleared immediately after the MAC_LPI_Control_Status register is read. This is because the clear signal, generated in CSR clock domain, has to cross the Rx clock domain, and then clear the interrupt source. This delay is at least four clock cycles of Rx clock and can be significant when the DWC_ether_qos is operating in the 10Mbps mode.
#### 10.6.3.5 Access Lock for DCRCC, RSF, and FEP in 1GMAC
At the receive side, packets, which violate MACsec security protocol are corrupted and sent to MAC with incorrect CRC. MAC must drop all such packets. But 1GMAC has the following configuration bits with which even incorrect CRC Packets can be taken into the system. MAC_Ext_Configuration.DCRCC ;; Disables CRC check MTL_RxQ(#i)_Operation_Mode.RSF ;;Queue is in cut-through mode and [ i = {0,1,2,…9}
- Receive queue number]
MTL_RxQ(#i)_Operation_Mode.FEP ;; Forward error packets and [ i = {0,1,2,…9} = Receive queue number]

1G Ethernet Controller Programming Guidelines Therefore, software access must block the register configuration bitsto ensure that MACSEC rejected packets are dropped in MAC. It is implemented using the Lock control bits in MACSEC TZ space as shown in the below diagram. MACSEC_MAC_CONTROL_0.DCRCC_LOCK = 1 access control bit in MACSEC MACSEC_MAC_CONTROL_0.RxQ_FEP_LOCK = 1 access control bit in MACSEC for all 10 queues MACSEC_MAC_CONTROL_0.RSF_LOCL = 1 access control bit in MACSEC for all 10 queues. The default value for Locks is “1." During normal operation, Trusted software (TZ entity) can remove the Lock, update the value of DCRC, FEP, and RSF to their secure state and apply the Lock. After Lock is applied, normal ETHER_QOS driver cannot update these values from normal world.
**Figure 10.40 Blocking the access to CRC Configuration bits in XGMAC**
The Lock Control bits are available only in TZ when TZ is active based on macsec_hw_tz_check fuse. During the bring-up phase, when the fuse is not blown, RM can access these LOCK bits and program them to “0”. Then the RM updates the value of DCRC, FEP, and RSF bits to their desired value. When the macsec_hw_tz_check fuse is blown, the TZ software only can set or reset these Lock bits.

1G Ethernet Controller Programming Guidelines
#### 10.6.3.6 DMA Channel Recovery Programming Guidelines
Steps to recover a DMA channel in an error condition (By reading DMA_CH(#i)_Status register) without affecting other channels. RM carries out the recovery steps. Tx Recovery 1. Stop the TX DMA (even when it is active state). Flush the corresponding MTL queue. Reprogram the DMA channel-specific registers. Start the DMA channel. a. b. c. d. Rx Recovery 2. Stop the RX DMA. Set the RPF bit so that all packets get flushed one after another (this would lead to packet drops for that queue). Reprogram the DMA channel-specific registers. Start the DMA channel. a. b. c. d.
#### 10.6.3.7 DMA/Queue Dynamic Change of Arbitration Rules
MTL Transmit Queues Arbitration “MTL_Operation_Mode.SCHALG” register field sets the Tx scheduling algorithm scheme. This value can be dynamically changed without any packet corruption. MTL Receive Queues Arbitration “MTL_Operation_Mode.RAA” register field sets the Rx scheduling algorithm scheme. This value can be dynamically changed without any packet corruption. Transmit DMA channels Arbitration “DMA_Mode.TAA” register field is used to select the arbitration scheme for transmit side when multiple TX DMA channels are enabled. This field can be changed dynamically.
#### 10.6.3.8 Golden Register Settings
The recommended values of some of the golden registers are shown. Table 10.16 Golden Register settings Register Field Value Comments DMA_Mode TXPR When 0, this bit indicates that RX DMA has higher priority over TX DMA during arbitration for system memory access. DMA_Mode PR The priority ratio is 1:1 WRR between RX and TX DMA arbitration requests.

1G Ethernet Controller Programming Guidelines
##### 10.6.3.8.1 Route Safety interrupt to LIC as common interrupt
The safety interrupts can be routed to the Ethernet software driver when the following bits are programmed: COMMON_INTR_MASK.EQOS_CORE_CORRECTABLE_ERR = 1 COMMON_INTR_MASK.EQOS_CORE_UNCORRECTABLE_ERR = 1
#### 10.6.3.9 Programming Guidelines to Operate 1GMAC in Loop-back Mode
For Internal loop-back mode, software has to configure ETHER_QOS_CLOCK_CTRL_0. RX_CLK_SEL register bit to 1 (LOOPBACK), with which Tx Clock is fed to RX domain in the CAR module. Disable the SLCG by programming ETHER_QOS_CLOCK_CTRL_0. ETHER_QOS_CLK_OVR_ON bit to 1.
#### 10.6.3.10 Programming Guidelines for Energy-Efficient Ethernet
The following register should be programmed in ETHER_QOS_Wrapper to enable clock gating needed for EEE functionality. ETHER_QOS_CLOCK_CTRL_0. ETHER_QOS_CLK_OVR_ON=0 During the DWC_ether_qos initialization, after you enable the (EEE) you can program how to enter and exit Tx LPI mode:
##### 10.6.3.10.1 Entering and Exiting the Tx LPI Mode
EEE enables the IEEE 802.3 Media Access Control (MAC) sub layer along with a family of Physical layers to operate in the Low-Power Idle (LPI) mode. In the Transmit path, the software must set the LPIEN bit of the MAC_LPI_Control_Status register to indicate to the MAC to stop transmission and initiate the LPI protocol. You can configure the (EEE) feature in coreConsultant while initializing the controller. Follow these steps while initializing DWC_ether_qos: 1. Read the PHY register through the MDIO interface, check if the remote end has the EEE capability, and then negotiate the timer values. Program the PHY registers through the MDIO interface (including the RX_CLK_stoppable bit that indicates to the PHY whether to stop Rx clock in LPI mode.) Program Bits[25:16] and Bits[15:0] in MAC_LPI_Timers_Control register. Read the link status of the PHY chip by using the MDIO interface and update Bit 17 of MAC_LPI_Control_Status accordingly. This update should be done whenever the link status in the PHY chip changes. Program the MAC_1US_Tic_Counter as per the frequency of the clock used for accessing the CSR slave port. 2. 3. 4. 5.

1G Ethernet Controller Programming Guidelines 6. Program the MAC_LPI_Entry_Timer register (LPIET) with the IDLE time for which the MAC should wait before entering the LPI state on its own. Set LPITE and LPITXA (bit[20:19]) of MAC_LPI_Control_Status register to enable the auto- entry into LPI and auto-exit of MAC from LPI state. Program the MAC_1US_Tic_Counter as per the frequency of the clock used for accessing the CSR slave port. Program the MAC_LPI_Entry_Timer register (LPIET) with the IDLE time for which the MAC should wait before entering the LPI state on its own. Set LPITE and LPITXA (bit[20:19]) of MAC_LPI_Control_Status register to enable the auto- entry into LPI and auto-exit of MAC from LPI state. Set Bit 16 of MAC_LPI_Control_Status register to make the MAC Transmitter enter the LPI state. The MAC enters the LPI mode after completing all scheduled packets and remains IDLE for the time indicated by LPIET. It sets the TLPIEN (bit[0]) after entry to LPI state. When a packet is scheduled for transmission (when the TxDMA comes out of IDLE state or when a packet is presented at ATI or MTI interface), the MAC Transmitter exits LPI state automatically. It waits for TWT time before setting the TLPIEX interrupt status bit and then resume the packet transmission. MAC Transmitter reenters LPI state if it remains IDLE for LPIET time and sets the TLPIEN bit and the entry-exit cycle continues. Reset LPITXEN if the application wants to override the auto-entry/exit modes and it wants to make the MAC Transmitter exit the LPI state directly. 7. 8. 9. 10. 11. 12. 13. 14. Notes: 1. To ensure that MAC enter the LPI state only after completion of transmission of all the queued frames in the Tx FIFO, you should set Bit 19 in MAC_LPI_Control_Status register. To turn off the GMII Transmit Clock during the LPI state, use the sbd_tx_clk_gating_ctrl_o signal for gating the clock input. 2. Table 10.17 Recommended Settings for Performance Settings Value Comments PBLx8 Enable eight times PBL mode. Each beat is 16 bytes. Multiple by 8 will make it 128 bytes. RxPBL Configure RX PBL to 1 KB. TxPBL Configure TX PBL to 1 KB. IPBL Disable Ignore PBL configuration. TSF All the transmit queues should be operated in store and forward mode. RSF All the receive queues should be operated in store and forward mode. Maximum Burst Length Maximum burst length supported by EQOS

1G Ethernet Controller Programming Guidelines Settings Value Comments RD_OSR_LMT Maximum AXI Read outstanding requests WR_OSR_LMT Maximum AXI Write outstanding requests
#### 10.6.3.11 Pad Calibration Programming Guidelines
ETHER_QOS padctrl registers are present in the registers section of this chapter.
##### 10.6.3.11.1 Programming Steps
1. 2. 3. Set PAD_E_INPUT_OR_E_PWRD = 1 in ETHER_QOS_SDMEMCOMPPADCTRL_0 register. Wait for 1 µs after PAD_E_INPUT_OR_E_PWRD is enabled. Set AUTO_CAL_START and AUTO_CAL_ENABLE to 1 in ETHER_QOS_AUTO_CAL_CONFIG_0 register. Wait for 1 µs. Wait for up to 10 ms for AUTO_CAL_ACTIVE in ETHER_QOS_AUTO_CAL_STATUS_0 register to become 0. If it is not 0 after 10 ms, software can assume auto-calibration has timed out. If it becomes zero within 10 ms, it is assumed that calibration has completed. Clear PAD_E_INPUT_OR_E_PWRD to save power. Software should not clear the AUTO_CAL_ENABLE in ETHER_QOS_AUTO_CAL_CONFIG_0 register after calibration. It should be set to 1 always to use the calibration codes generated by the calibration controller. 4. 5. 6. 7.
#### 10.6.3.12 Pad Recalibration Programming Guidelines
##### 10.6.3.12.1 Programming Steps
1. Disable the interrupt RGSMIIIE bit in the MAC_Interrupt_Enable register (to avoid LNKSTS interrupt triggered due to Rx pad disable/enable. In software ISR, for LNKSTS interrupt, read the MAC_PHYIF_Control_Status values and update speed and mode for MAC controller.) Disable the Transmit DMA by clearing Bit 0 (ST) of DMA_CH(#i)_TX_Control (for i = 0;i <= DWC_EQOS_NUM_DMA_TX_CH-1) Register. Wait for any previous frame transmissions to complete. You can check this by reading the appropriate bits of MTL_TxQ0_Debug register (TRCSTS is not 01 and TXQSTS=0). Disable the MAC transmitter and the MAC receiver by clearing Bit (RE) and Bit 1(TE) of the MAC_Configuration register. Disable the Receive DMA, after making sure that the data in the Rx FIFO is transferred to the system memory (by reading the appropriate bits of MTL_RxQ0_Debug register, PRXQ=0 and RXQSTS=00). 2. 3. 4. 5.

1G Ethernet Controller Programming Guidelines 6. Stop read/write to the PHY registers (MDIO interface) and check MDIO idle state with MAC_MDIO_Address register bit0 (GB). Check the MAC_Debug register for a value for 0x0 to make sure that MII interface is idle. Disable the Rx Pad pins (PADCTL_EQOS_EQOS_RDx reg E_INPUT bit =0, where x =0,1,2,3 and PADCTL_EQOS_EQOS_RX_CTL_0 reg E_INPUT bit =0) Do pad calibration. Enable the Rx pad pins (PADCTL_EQOS_EQOS_RDx reg E_INPUT bit =1, where x =0,1,2,3 and PADCTL_EQOS_EQOS_RX_CTL_0 reg E_INPUT bit =1) 7. 8. 9. 10. a. Read the MAC_PHY_Control_Status register to clear any pending interrupts due to enable Rx pad pins. 11. 12. 13. Start the Tx/Rx DMA channels. Enable the MAC Transmitter and Receiver (MAC_config TE/RE bits). Enable interrupt RGSMIIIE bit in MAC_Interrupt_Enable register.
#### 10.6.3.13 Other Guidelines
The following guideline forwards all dropped packets to software. 1. To forward all the packets that are discarded by the (L2, VLAN, L3 and L4) filtering logic: Program MAC_Packet_Filter.RA bit to 1. To forward packets that have CRC Errors: Program MTL_RxQ0_Operation_Mode.FEP bit to 1. To forward undersized good packets (no CRC error but length < 64 bytes): Program MTL_RxQ0_Operation_Mode.FUP bit to 1. 2. 3. The following guideline is for GCL Programming: 1. Software programs the Cycle time greater than the first-time interval in GCL for the proper functioning of Qbv. Software programs the following bit in the 1GMAC Core register to enable this interrupt. 2. a. MTL_EST_Intr_Enable.CGCE = 1
#### 10.6.3.14 Miscellaneous Programming Guidelines
In the receive path, all preemptable queues should be operated in store and forward mode. At the Transmit side, packets coming out of 1GMAC/XGMAC must have an additional IPG plus the minimum IPG (12 bytes) mentioned by the standard. The additional IPG is required to insert MACsec headers in the transmitting packets. It can be either: 24 bytes (8 bytes SECTAG + 16 bytes ICV) 32 bytes (16 bytes SECTAG + 16 bytes ICV) The Reside Queue (RQ) field (of MAC_RxQ_Ctrl1 register) should be programmed with a non- zero value as Q0 is the default queue for express packets.

1G Ethernet Controller Registers The MSS field in the DMA_CH(#i)_Control register when TSO is enabled should be programmed as follows. Max MSS: MSS+header should be equal to half the programmed Tx Queue size. The header length plus the MSS size (which is equal to the size of each TCP segment) must not exceed 16383. Min MSS: Configured value should be greater than configured data width in bytes. Recommended to use 64 B. Program the following register for Tx Queue VLAN tag insertion in the transmit packet. MAC_VLAN_Incl(#i) (for i = 0; i <= DWC_EQOS_NUM_TXQ-1) Program MISCREG_PADCTLREG_APE_PTP_CLK_MUX_SEL_0 to select the PTP Timestamp to be used in APE module. Safety interrupts are routed to the HSM module by default. They are also routed as common interrupt to LIC module when enabled. The following register should be programmed for this functionality ETHER_QOS_COMMON_INTR_ENABLE_0 Perform the following steps before issuing soft reset. a.
